Razi's Second Sophism: Conflicting Tawatur Reports
Razi presents contradictory tawatur examples and argues that either they are true or tawatur fails.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses examples of contradictory tawatur reports from Magians, Jews, and Christians to argue that tawatur cannot be an independent source of certainty.

Core Idea
If tawatur gives knowledge, contradictory false reports would be true; ergo tawatur fails.

In this passage, Razi presents a powerful objection against the reliability of tawatur. He brings three examples from different religious communities that all claim miraculous foundations. This forces a dilemma: either those false reports are true (which can't be) or tawatur isn't certain. Razi then answers the expected counterargument, showing that rational proofs must override tawatur.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the three examples: Magians, Jews, Christians.
2
Identify the three examples
Razi lists three groups that transmit reports: Magians about Zoroaster, Jews about Moses' law never being abrogated, Christians about Jesus being divine and crucified. Note that all three are considered false in Islamic theology.
3
Understand the dilemma
Razi presents a dilemma: if tawatur produces knowledge, then these false reports would be true, which is impossible. If it doesn't produce knowledge, then tawatur is useless as a source of certainty.
This dilemma challenges the reliability of tawatur.
4
Examine the objection and Razi's response
The objection says: rational proofs refute those reports, but no rational proof refutes tawatur about Muhammad. Razi's response: that actually strengthens his argument, because it shows that rational proofs can override tawatur, meaning tawatur alone is not sufficient.
Razi turns the objection into evidence for his point.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this means: tawatur reports must be evaluated against rational proofs. Tawatur is not self-sufficient; it requires rational support to be accepted.
This connects to broader debates about epistemology in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثانية: أنا نرى المجوس على كثرتهم وتفرقهم في الشرق والغرب يخبرون عن المعجزات العظيمة لـ "زرادشت مع أنه كان كذابًا ساحرًا عندكم. وأيضا : اليهود على كثرتهم وتفرقهم في الشرق والغرب يخبرون أن موسى ال قال : إن شريعتي لا تصير منسوخة البتة. وأيضا : النصارى على كثرتهم وتفرقهم في الشرق والغرب يخبرون أن عيسى كان يقول : يثالث ثلاثة - سبحانه وتعالى عما يشركون - وبأنه ابن الله ويخبرون ان اليهود صلبوا عيسى وقتلوه، فإن كان التواتر مفيدًا للعلم فقد صحت هذه الأخبار، ويلزم من صحتها الطعن في نبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وإن كانت غير مفيدة للعلم فحينئذ خرج التواتر عن كونه مفيدا للعلم. لا يقال : إنما دفعنا هذه الأقوال لقيام الدلائل العقلية على أنها باطلة، فأما التواتر عن وجود محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن إدعائه الرسالة فإنه لم تقم الدلالة على بطلانه، فظهر الفرق، لأنا نقول : هذا القدر يقوي كلامنا ؛ لأن خبر التواتر لما حصل في تلك الصور ثم قامت الدلائل القاطعة على بطلانها، فحينئذٍ ثبت أن الدلائل القاطعة قامت على بطلان خبر التواتر في هذه الصورة، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ثبت أنه لا يمكن الاستدلال بخبر التواتر على المخبر عنه حق وصدق.
The second sophism: We see the Magians, despite their multitude and dispersal in East and West, relating about the great miracles of Zoroaster - while he was, according to you, a liar and a sorcerer. Also the Jews, despite their multitude and dispersal in East and West, relate that Moses said: 'My religion will never be abrogated at all.' Also the Christians, despite their multitude and dispersal in East and West, relate that Jesus used to say: 'Three' - exalted is He above what they associate - and that he is the son of God, and they relate that the Jews crucified Jesus and killed him. If tawatur is productive of knowledge, then these reports are true, and from their truth follows impugning the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him. And if it is not productive of knowledge, then tawatur ceases to be productive of knowledge. It cannot be said: 'We only refute these statements because rational proofs establish that they are false; as for the tawatur about the existence of Muhammad and his claim to prophethood, no proof of its falsehood has been established, so the difference is clear.' For we say: This point strengthens our argument. Because when the tawatur report occurred in those cases and then decisive proofs established its falsehood, then it is established that decisive proofs have established the falsehood of the tawatur report in that instance. If the matter is so, it is established that it is not possible to use tawatur report as evidence that what is reported is true and genuine.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This is the second sophism of the second maqam. It brings examples: the Magi report miracles of Zoroaster (whom Muslims consider a liar), the Jews report that Moses said his law would never be abrogated, the Christians report that Jesus said he is one of three, that he is the son of God, and that he was crucified. If tawatur produces knowledge, then these reports would be true, which contradicts Islamic belief. If it does not produce knowledge, then tawatur is not a source of certainty. A possible objection: these reports are rejected because rational proofs show them false, whereas the tawatur about Muhammad is not contradicted by rational proofs. The answer: this actually strengthens the argument because the alleged tawatur reports were defeated by rational proofs, proving that tawatur alone cannot establish truth; rational proofs can override it, so tawatur is not an independent source of certainty.

Key Terms
المجوس
اليهود
النصارى
التواتر
الدلائل العقلية
المنسوخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is about disproving Judaism, Christianity, or Zoroastrianism.
Correction: The argument is purely about the epistemological value of tawatur. Razi uses these examples to show that tawatur cannot be an independent source of certainty, regardless of the truth of the specific reports.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does Razi draw from the examples of Magian, Jewish, and Christian tawatur reports?
A) That those reports are true.
B) That tawatur cannot be trusted because it can convey falsehood.
C) That those reports are not actually tawatur.
D) That rational proofs are unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that tawatur alone cannot guarantee truth, because rational proofs can override even broadly transmitted reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief that is widely held in your community, do you automatically consider it true, or do you examine it against rational proofs as Razi demands? Which areas of your faith might be based on mere tawatur rather than certainty?
?
If you were faced with a widespread report that contradicted clear rational evidence, would you have the courage to reject it, even if it meant going against the majority? How does this lesson prepare you for such a test?
?
Razi shows that even tawatur can be wrong. Is there any belief you hold that you have never questioned because 'everyone says it'? What would it take for you to subject that belief to the same scrutiny Razi applies here?

Ten Character Miracles of the Prophet
Razi enumerates ten traits of the Prophet that constitute sensory miracles of the third division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten character miracles of the Prophet Muhammad that Razi presents as sensory miracles of the third division.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character traits are miracles no human could combine.

Razi now turns to a third division of sensory miracles: those found in the Prophet's character. He enumerates ten traits that, in their unprecedented combination, prove his prophethood. Each trait is supported by scriptural evidence and reason. This lesson walks through these ten qualities and their miraculous nature.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recognise that Razi is listing sensory miracles of the third division, which relate to the Prophet's attributes and character.
These are not just moral virtues; they are presented as miracles.
2
Read the ten qualities individually
Read each of the ten traits in the Arabic and translation. Notice the specific Quranic verses cited as evidence for each.
3
Reflect on the cumulative argument
Consider the final point: that the combination of all these perfections in one person is unprecedented and itself a miracle.
This is the key argument—the whole is greater than the sum of its parts.
4
Connect to prophethood
Ask yourself: How does this collection of traits serve as a proof of prophethood? Why would these traits be impossible for an impostor to sustain over a lifetime?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالأول: أن أحدًا ما سمع في مهمات الدين ولا في مهمات الدنيا كذبًا البتة، فلو صدر عنه الكذب مرة واحدة لاجتهد أعداؤه في تشهيره وإظهاره. والثاني: أنه ما أقدم على فعل قبيح لا قبل النبوة ولا بعدها. الثالث: أنه لم يفر عن أحد من أعدائه لا قبل النبوة ولا بعدها - وإن عظم الخوف - مثل يوم الأحزاب، وهذا يدل على أنه كان قوي القلب بمواعيد الله، حيث قال: ﴿ وَاللهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٧] وقال: ﴿حَسْبَكَ الله﴾ [الأنفال: ٦٢] وقال: ﴿إِلَّا نَصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللهُ﴾ [التوبة: ٤٠]. الرابع: أنه كان عظيم الشفقة والرحمة على أمته، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ﴾ [فاطر: ٨] وقال تعالى: ﴿فَلَعَلَّكَ بَخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ﴾ [الكهف: ٦] وقال: ﴿عَلَيْهِمُ الْجَ؟﴾ [الحجر: ٨٨] وقال: ﴿عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ حَرِيصٌ عَلَيْكُمْ﴾ [التوبة: ١٢٨]. الخامس: أنه كان في أعظم الدرجات في السخاوة، حتى إنه تعالى عاتبه عليها وقال: ﴿وَلَا تَجْعَلْ يَدَكَ مَغْلُولَةً إِلَى عُنُقِكَ وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ﴾ [الإسراء: ٢٩]. السادس: أنه ما كان للدنيا في قلبه وقع، وأن قريشاً عرضوا عليه المال والزوجة والرياسة حتى يترك هذه الدعوى فلم يلتفت إليهم. السابع: أنه كان في غاية الفصاحة، كما قال: «أوتيت جوامع الكلم». الثامن: أنه بقي على طريقته المرضية من أول عمره إلى آخره، والكذب المزور لا يمكنه ذلك، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ مَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُتَكَلِّفِينَ﴾ [ص: ٨٦]. التاسع: أنه كان مع أهل الدنيا والثروة في غاية الترفع، ومع الفقراء والمساكين وأهل الدين في غاية التواضع. العاشر: أنه لو كان في كل واحدة من هذه الصفات والأخلاق في الغاية القصوى من الكمال - كان مستجمعاً لها بأسرها - ولم يتفق ذلك لأحد من الخلق، فكان اجتماعها في ذاته من أعظم المعجزات.
The first: that no one ever heard from him a lie in important matters of religion or worldly matters at all. So if a lie had occurred from him once, his enemies would have striven to publicize it and make it known. The second: that he never committed a reprehensible act, neither before prophethood nor after it. The third: that he never fled from any of his enemies, neither before prophethood nor after it, even when fear was great, such as on the Day of the Confederates. This indicates that he was strong of heart through the promises of Allah, where He said: 'And Allah will protect you from the people' [5:67], and He said: 'Allah is sufficient for you' [8:62], and He said: 'If you do not help him, Allah has already helped him' [9:40]. The fourth: that he was extremely compassionate and merciful towards his ummah. Allah Almighty said: 'So do not let your soul go out in grief over them' [35:8], and He said: 'Perhaps you will kill yourself with grief' [18:6], and He said: [??] and He said: 'Grievous to him is what you suffer; eager for you' [9:128]. The fifth: that he was at the highest degree of generosity, so much so that the Almighty rebuked him for it and said: 'And do not make your hand chained to your neck nor extend it completely' [17:29]. The sixth: that the world had no place in his heart, and that Quraysh offered him wealth, marriage, and leadership so that he would abandon this claim, but he did not pay attention to them. The seventh: that he was extremely eloquent, as he said: 'I have been given the comprehensive words.' The eighth: that he remained upon his approved way from the beginning of his life to its end. False lying is not possible for him. To this refers the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Say, I do not ask you for any reward for it, nor am I of the pretenders' [38:86]. The ninth: that he was in the utmost degree of elevation with the people of the world and wealth, and in the utmost degree of humility with the poor, the destitute, and the people of religion. The tenth: that if each one of these qualities and morals was at the ultimate peak of perfection—and he combined all of them—and this has not occurred for anyone among creation, then their combination in his essence is among the greatest miracles.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration. The author lists ten specific traits of the Prophet that are considered part of the third division of sensory miracles, i.e., miracles pertaining to his attributes. These traits are: (1) the absence of any lie ever heard from him; (2) his avoidance of any evil act before and after prophethood; (3) his unparalleled bravery and steadfastness in battle, supported by divine promises; (4) his extreme compassion and mercy for his community, as described in the Quran; (5) his extraordinary generosity, even to the point of divine rebuke to moderate it; (6) his complete disinterest in worldly goods and power; (7) his eloquence as the recipient of 'jami' al-kalim' (comprehensive speech); (8) his consistency in the best way of life from beginning to end, which precludes falsehood; (9) his perfect balance of humility with the poor and dignity with the wealthy; (10) the unprecedented combination of all these perfections in one person, which itself constitutes a miracle.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These traits are simply good moral qualities that any person could have.
Correction: They are miracles because their combination in one person is unprecedented and impossible without divine aid.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's ten character traits, supported by Quranic verses, collectively form a sensory miracle that validates his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the Prophet's truthfulness was so absolute that no lie was ever heard from him, would the same be said of you by those who know you best? This week, in what conversation are you most tempted to stretch the truth? What will it cost you to speak it plainly?
?
The Prophet combined all ten perfections; you struggle with even one. Does that disparity humble you or move you to action? Decide now one small, measurable change you will make starting tomorrow to mirror him in that trait.

The First Intellectual Miracle: Knowledge Without Learning
Razi enumerates the first type of intellectual miracle: the Prophet's knowledge despite illiteracy and lack of education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's comprehensive knowledge, despite his lack of formal education and his non-scholarly environment, constitutes an intellectual miracle that validates his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge arose from a divine source, not human learning.

This passage presents the first of six intellectual miracles: the Prophet's remarkable knowledge of theology and history, which came without any teacher or scholarly environment. Razi invites us to consider the Prophet's background and his profound output as a clear sign of divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the detailed description of the Prophet's environment.
Pay attention to the emphasis on the lack of scholars and the Prophet's limited travel.
2
Identify the elements of the miracle
Note what is miraculous: a) lack of learning environment, b) limited travel and no teachers, c) yet the Prophet produced profound knowledge of Allah and accurate history.
3
Understand the proof of authenticity
The passage emphasizes that the Prophet's knowledge matches the Quran and historical accounts perfectly, and he even challenged his opponents to mubahala.
This shows the knowledge is not humanly attainable under these conditions.
4
Reflect on the implication
This miracle serves as a rational proof of prophethood: a person without education could not produce such knowledge unless taught by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المعجزات العقلية فهي ستة أنواع : النوع الأول : أنه إنما ظهر في قبيلة ما كان أهلها من أهل العلم، وكانوا من بلدة ما كان فيها أحد من العلماء وكانت الجهالة غالبة عليهم، ولم يتفق له سفر من تلك البلدة إلا مرتين إلى الشام وكانت مدة تلك المسافرة قليلة، ولم يذهب الأحد من العلماء والحكماء إلى تلك البلدة حتى يقال : إنه تعلم العلم من الحكيم. ذلك فإذا خرج من مثل هذه البلدة ومن مثل هذه القبيلة إنسان من غير أن مارس شيئًا من العلوم، ولا تتلمذ لأحد من العلماء البتة، ثم بلغ في معرفة ذات الله وصفاته وأفعاله وأسمائه وأحكامه هذا المبلغ الذي عجز جميع الأذكياء من العقلاء عن القرب منه، وأقر الكل بأنه لا يمكن أن لا يمكن أن يزداد في تقرير الدلائل على ما ورد في القرآن، ثم ذكر قصص الأولين وتواريخ المتقدمين، بحيث لم يتمكن أحد من الأعداء أن يقول : إنه أخطأ في شيء منها، بل بلغ كلامه في البعد عن الريب والشك إلى أن قال عند مجادلتهم إياه : فَقُلْ تَعَالَوْا نَدْعُ أَبْنَاءَنَا وَأَبْنَاء كُو [آل عمران: ٦١] إلى قوله : فَنَجْعَل لَعَنَتَ اللهِ عَلَى الْكَذِبِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ٦١] وقال : وتِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ
As for the intellectual miracles, they are six types: The first type: that he appeared in a tribe whose people were not people of knowledge, and they were from a town in which there was none of the scholars, and ignorance dominated them. He did not travel from that town except twice to Syria, and the duration of those travels was short. No scholar or wise man went to that town so that it could be said that he learned knowledge from a sage. So when there emerged from such a town and such a tribe a human being, without having practiced any of the sciences, nor having been a student of any scholar at all, then he reached in knowledge of the essence of Allah, His attributes, His actions, His names, and His rulings to such a level that all the intelligent and wise are incapable of approaching it, and all acknowledge that it is not possible to increase in the presentation of proofs beyond what is in the Quran. Then he mentioned the stories of the ancients and the histories of earlier peoples, such that none of the enemies could say that he had made a mistake in any of them. Rather, his speech reached such a level of freedom from doubt and suspicion that when they argued with him, he said: 'Come, let us call our sons and your sons...' up to his saying: 'and make the curse of Allah upon the liars' [3:61]. And he said: 'That is from the news of the unseen...'
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage discusses the first type of intellectual miracle. The author argues that the Prophet Muhammad came from a tribe and a city lacking scholars and knowledge. He did not travel extensively nor study under any teacher. Despite this, he produced knowledge about the essence and attributes of Allah, His actions, names, and rulings, to a degree that the most intelligent people cannot match. Furthermore, he accurately recounted stories of previous nations and historical events without error. His arguments in debates were so compelling that he could challenge his opponents to mutual imprecation (mubahala). This combination of comprehensive knowledge, historical accuracy, and dialectical skill, originating from an unlearned person in an unlearned environment, is a clear intellectual miracle.

Key Terms
المعجزات العقلية
مباهلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The intellectual miracle is only about the Quran's eloquence.
Correction: Razi highlights that the miracle also includes the Prophet's deep theological understanding and accurate historical knowledge, all learned without human instruction.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why is the Prophet's knowledge considered an intellectual miracle?
A) He was illiterate
B) He came from a non-scholarly environment
C) His knowledge surpassed that of all scholars
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's knowledge, originating from an unlettered man in an uneducated environment, is a rational miracle proving his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) gained deep knowledge of Allah without any human teacher, while you have access to scholars, books, and endless resources. What is your excuse for not seeking that same knowledge? This week, commit to learning one new thing about Allah's attributes from the Quran or Sunnah and act upon it.
?
The Prophet was so certain of his message that he could challenge his opponents to a mutual curse. How certain are you that the Islam you follow is the truth? Are your beliefs built on evidence or just inherited habit? What is one area of your faith you are unsure about, and what step will you take to resolve that doubt?
?
The Prophet's historical knowledge was flawless, even though he had no formal education. In contrast, how much of your religious knowledge comes from reliable sources? Are you willing to verify what you know against the Quran and authentic hadith? Choose one belief or practice you've taken for granted and research its evidence until you are satisfied.

Six Moral Miracles of the Prophet
Six moral miracles of the Prophet enumerated by Imam al-Razi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six moral miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) as presented by Imam al-Razi, and why their combination is itself a miracle.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character combines six perfect qualities that no liar could sustain.

Imam al-Razi continues his enumeration of the miraculous aspects of the Prophet's life by turning to his moral character. Each quality listed here is not only admirable in itself, but together they form a cumulative argument that only a true prophet could embody such consistent perfection. This passage presents six specific moral miracles from the fifth to the tenth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the sequential enumeration from fifth to tenth.
The passage is a list; each point is a separate proof.
2
Identify each moral quality
Go through each quality: generosity, indifference to world, eloquence, consistency, humility with dignity, and the combination of all.
These are not just good traits; they are presented as miracles.
3
Connect each to prophetic truth
Reflect on why each quality could not be sustained by a liar. For example, consistency over a lifetime is argued impossible for a pretender.
Imam al-Razi uses Quranic verses to support some points.
4
Understand the cumulative miracle
The tenth point concludes that the combination of all these perfections in one person is itself a miracle, as no human has ever combined them.
This is the key takeaway: the sum is greater than the parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : أنه كان في أعظم الدرجات في السخاوة حتى إنه تعالى عاتبه عليها وقال : ﴿وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ﴾ [الإسراء: ٢٩] . والسادس : أنه ما كان للدنيا في قلبه وقع ، وأن قريشا عرضوا عليه المال والزوجة والرياسة حتى يترك هذه الدعوى فلم يلتفت إليهم . السابع : أنه كان في غاية الفصاحة ، كما قال : أوتيت جوامع الكلم . والثامن : أنه بقي على طريقته المرضية من أول عمره إلى آخره . والكذب المزور لا يمكنه ذلك ، وإليه الإشارة بقوله تعالى : ﴿قُلْ مَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُتَكَلِّفِينَ﴾ [ص: ٨٦] . والتاسع : أنه كان مع أهل الدنيا والثروة في غاية الترفع ومع الفقراء والمساكين وأهل الدين في غاية التواضع . والعاشر : أنه لو كان في كل واحدة من هذه الصفات والأخلاق في الغاية القصوى من الكمال - كان مستجمعا لها بأسرها - ولم يتفق ذلك لأحد من الخلق ، فكان اجتماعها في ذاته من أعظم المعجزات.
Fifth: That he was in the highest degrees of generosity, so much so that Allah Almighty rebuked him for it and said: 'And do not stretch it out completely' [Al-Isra: 29]. Sixth: That the world had no place in his heart, and that Quraysh offered him wealth, wives, and leadership so that he would abandon this claim, but he did not pay attention to them. Seventh: That he was in the utmost eloquence, as he said: 'I have been given the comprehensive words.' Eighth: That he remained on his approved path from the beginning of his life to the end. And the forged lie cannot do that, and to that is the indication of His saying: 'Say: I do not ask you for any reward for it, nor am I of the pretenders' [Sad: 86]. Ninth: That he was with the people of the world and wealth in the utmost elevation, and with the poor, the needy, and the people of religion in the utmost humility. Tenth: That if he were in each of these attributes and qualities at the ultimate peak of perfection—he was encompassing all of them—and that did not occur for anyone from creation, so their combination in his person is among the greatest miracles.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage enumerates six moral miracles of the Prophet (from the fifth to the tenth), each demonstrating a unique aspect of his character that would be impossible for a liar to maintain consistently. The fifth is his extreme generosity, even rebuked by Allah for giving too freely. The sixth is his indifference to worldly temptations, rejecting Quraysh's offers. The seventh is his eloquence, receiving 'comprehensive speech'. The eighth is his lifelong consistency on the right path, impossible for a pretender. The ninth is his balance between humility and dignity. The tenth concludes that the combination of all these perfect qualities in one person is itself a miracle.

Key Terms
السخاوة
الفصاحة
الترفع
التواضع
المعجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Each of these qualities alone is a separate miracle independent of the others.
Correction: While each quality is remarkable, the passage emphasizes that the combination of all six in one person is what constitutes the greatest miracle, as no other human has possessed them all together.

Checkpoint
What does the fifth moral quality highlight about the Prophet?
A) His eloquence
B) His generosity
C) His humility
D) His consistency

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's moral perfection, as a combination of six extraordinary qualities, is itself a miraculous proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these six moral qualities is most absent from your character today? What specific situation this week can you use to practice one aspect of the Prophet's example?
?
The Prophet remained consistent from youth to old age. Where in your life do you find inconsistency between what you believe and what you do? What is one belief you hold that you are not acting on, and what will you do about it by tomorrow?
?
If the combination of these qualities is a miracle from Allah, what does that imply about your own attempts to cultivate even one of them? Are you relying on your own strength or seeking divine help? How will you change your approach starting now?

First Intellectual Miracle: Knowledge from Ignorance
Imam al-Razi proves prophethood from the Prophet's knowledge despite his illiterate background.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses the Prophet's illiterate environment and his subsequent profound knowledge as an intellectual miracle proving prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge, born from ignorance, is a clear sign of divine teaching.

Imam al-Razi presents six intellectual miracles; this first one focuses on the Prophet's background. He was born and raised in a tribe and town devoid of scholars, with no formal education or travel. Yet he produced the Qur'an and knowledge of the unseen that no human could attain. This lesson examines the steps of this argument and the Quranic evidence supporting it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the key conditions: the tribe's ignorance, lack of teachers, and the Prophet's lack of travel.
2
Identify the argument's structure
The passage first establishes the Prophet's environment, then describes his comprehensive knowledge, and finally cites Quranic verses as confirmation. See how each part builds the case.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Reflect on the final sentence: 'these states are not facilitated except by divine teaching.' This is the logical conclusion.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to see if you grasped the core proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المعجزات العقلية فهي ستة أنواع : النوع الأول : أنه إنما ظهر في قبيلة ما كان أهلها من أهل العلم ، وكانوا من بلدة ما كان فيها أحد من العلماء وكانت الجهالة غالبة عليهم ، ولم يتفق له سفر من تلك البلدة إلا مرتين إلى الشام وكانت مدة تلك المسافرة قليلة ، ولم يذهب أحد من العلماء والحكماء إلى تلك البلدة حتى يقال : إنه تعلم العلم من ذلك الحكيم . فإذا خرج من مثل هذه البلدة ومن مثل هذه القبيلة إنسان من غير أن مارس شيئًا من العلوم ، ولا تتلمذ لأحد من العلماء البتة ، ثم بلغ في معرفة ذات الله وصفاته وأفعاله وأسمائه وأحكامه هذا المبلغ الذي عجز جميع الأذكياء من العقلاء عن القرب منه ، وأقر الكل بأنه لا يمكن أن يزداد في تقرير الدلائل على ما ورد في القرآن ، ثم ذكر قصص الأولين وتواريخ المتقدمين ، بحيث لم يتمكن أحد من الأعداء أن يقول : إنه أخطأ في شيء منها ، بل بلغ كلامه في البعد عن الريب والشك إلى أن قال عند مجادلتهم إياه : ﴿فَقُلْ تَعَالَوْا نَدْعُ أَبْنَاءَنَا وَأَبْنَاءَكُمْ﴾ [آل عمران: ٦١] إلى قوله : ﴿فَنَجْعَل لَّعْنَتَ اللَّهِ عَلَى الْكَاذِبِينَ﴾ [آل عمران: ٦١] وقال : ﴿وَتِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ مَا كُنتَ تَعْلَمُهَا أَنتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ﴾ [هود: ٤٩] ولم يقدر أحد أن يقول : إنه طالع كتاباً أو تتلمذ على أستاذ . وكانت هذه الأحوال الظاهرة معلومة للأصدقاء والأعداء على ما قال تعالى : ﴿أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ مُنكِرُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون: ٦٩] وقال : ﴿وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُو مِن قَبْلِهِ مِن كِتَابٍ وَلَا تَخُطُّهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذًا لَّارْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٤٨] وقال : ﴿فَقَدْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ عُمُرًا مِّن قَبْلِهِ أَفَلَا تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [يونس: ١٦] وكل من له عقل سليم وطبع مستقيم يعلم أن هذه الأحوال لا تتيسر إلا بالتعليم الإلهي والهداية الربانية.
As for the intellectual miracles, they are six types. The first type: That he emerged in a tribe whose people were not people of knowledge, and they were from a town in which there was none of the scholars, and ignorance prevailed over them, and he did not travel from that town except twice to Syria, and the duration of those journeys was short, and none of the scholars and wise men went to that town such that it could be said: He learned knowledge from that wise man. So when there emerged from such a town and from such a tribe a person who had never practiced any of the sciences, nor studied under any of the scholars at all, then he reached in knowledge of the Essence of Allah, His attributes, His acts, His names, and His rulings this level at which all the intelligent among the rational people fell short of approaching, and all acknowledged that it is impossible to increase in the presentation of proofs beyond what came in the Qur'an, then he recounted the stories of the earlier peoples and the histories of the ancients, such that none of the enemies could say that he erred in anything of them, rather his speech reached such a degree of being far from doubt and suspicion that he said when arguing with them: 'So say: Come, let us call our sons and your sons' [Al 'Imran: 61] to His words: 'and we will make the curse of Allah upon the liars' [Al 'Imran: 61], and he said: 'And these are from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know them, neither you nor your people' [Hud: 49], and no one was able to say that he had reviewed a book or studied under a teacher. And these apparent states were known to friends and enemies, as He, Most High, said: 'But do they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' [Al-Mu'minun: 69], and He said: 'And you did not recite before it any book, nor did you write it with your right hand, otherwise the falsifiers would have doubted' [Al-'Ankabut: 48], and He said: 'I have dwelt among you a lifetime before it, so do you not reason?' [Yunus: 16]. And everyone of sound intellect and upright nature knows that these states are not facilitated except by divine teaching and lordly guidance.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents the first intellectual miracle: the Prophet's origin and environment were utterly devoid of learning, yet he displayed unmatched knowledge of God, the Qur'an, and ancient histories. The argument proceeds step by step: the Prophet came from a non-learned tribe and town, with minimal travel and no known teachers. Despite this, he produced a level of knowledge that all intellects fall short of. Moreover, the Qur'an's challenge, including the Mubahala verse, and his accurate accounts of the unseen are impossible without divine revelation. The passage concludes with Quranic verses affirming his illiteracy and the fact that he lived among them for forty years without such speech, proving it must be from Allah.

Key Terms
المعجزات العقلية
التعليم الإلهي
الهداية الربانية
الجهالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the miracle is about his moral character or his ability to perform physical wonders.
Correction: The argument here is specifically about his knowledge arising from an ignorant background, not his character or other miracles.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof in the first intellectual miracle?
A) The Prophet's wealth
B) The Prophet's knowledge despite his illiterate environment
C) The Prophet's military victories
D) The Prophet's lineage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's knowledge, emerging from an illiterate environment, is a compelling intellectual miracle that can only be explained by divine teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet gained all his knowledge from Allah despite having no formal education. Are there areas in your life where you too easily accept ignorance, hiding behind your circumstances or lack of opportunity? What is one step you can take this week to learn something about your faith that you have avoided?
?
The Qur'an says about the Prophet: 'you did not know them, neither you nor your people.' Is there something you claim to know about Islam or about yourself that you have not actually learned from Allah through careful study and reflection? How would your life change if you honestly admitted that ignorance and sought His teaching?
?
Al-Razi concludes that these states 'are not facilitated except by divine teaching.' Do you truly live as though your understanding of Allah comes only through His guidance, or do you rely on your own intellect and effort? In your next prayer, will you specifically ask Allah to teach you what you need to know about Him?

The Prophet's Sudden Eloquence as an Intellectual Miracle
Imam al-Razi argues that the Prophet's sudden eloquence after forty years of silence is a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses the Prophet's forty years of silence and his sudden, inimitable eloquence to prove that his prophethood is from Allah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's lack of prior study and his sudden, unmatched speech prove it is from revelation.

Imam al-Razi presents a second intellectual miracle: the Prophet's sudden acquisition of profound religious knowledge after forty years without prior engagement. He argues that if the Prophet had studied, his enemies would have used that against him. Their silence proves he did not, and the unmatched quality of his speech points to divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation, to get a sense of the argument's flow.
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'لو' and 'لما'.
2
Identify the two key premises
The passage rests on two premises: (a) the Prophet had no prior engagement with these topics, and (b) the enemies did not accuse him of study. Find where each is stated.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
Al-Razi concludes that the only explanation for such sudden, inimitable speech is divine revelation. Note how he uses the passage of six hundred years without successful opposition.
This is an inductive argument from silence and accomplishment.
4
Reflect on the lasting challenge
Consider the significance that nearly six hundred years had passed without anyone producing similar speech. How does this strengthen the argument?
This adds a temporal dimension to the miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني : أنه لو كان قبل إظهار دعوى الرسالة والنبوة ما كان يشرع في هذه المسائل الإلهية وما كان يبحث عنها وما جرى على لسانه قط حديث النبوة والرسالة . والذي يدل على صحة قولنا : أنه لو اتفق أنه شرع في هذه المطالب والمباحث قبل إظهار ادعاء الرسالة والنبوة لقالت الكفار له : إنك أفنيت عمرك في التدبر والتأمل وتحصيل هذه الكلمات حتى قدرت الآن على إظهارها ، ولما لم يذكر هذا الكلام الأعداء مع شدة حرصهم على الطعن فيه وفي نبوته علمنا أنه ما كان شارعا قبل إظهار النبوة في شيء من هذه العلوم ، ومعلوم أن من انقضى من عمره أربعون سنة ولم يخض في شيء من هذه المطالب العلمية ثم إنه خاض بها دفعة واحدة ، وأتى بكلام عجز الأولون والآخرون عن معارضته بل قد انقضى الآن قريب من ستمائة سنة وما جاء أحد يمكنه إقامة المعارضة فصريح العقل يشهد بأن هذا لا يكون إلا على سبيل الوحي والتنزيل.
The second type: That before he declared the claim of messengership and prophethood, he had not engaged in these divine matters, nor had he investigated them, nor had the talk of prophethood and messengership ever occurred on his tongue. And that which indicates the correctness of our statement: that if it had happened that he had engaged in these topics and investigations before declaring the claim of messengership and prophethood, the disbelievers would have said to him: 'You have spent your life in reflection, contemplation, and acquisition of these words until you are now able to produce them.' And since the enemies did not mention this speech, despite their intense desire to attack him and his prophethood, we know that he was not engaged before declaring prophethood in any of these sciences. And it is known that one who has spent forty years of his life and not delved into any of these scholarly topics, then he delves into them all at once, and produces speech that the earlier and later generations are incapable of opposing—indeed nearly six hundred years have passed and no one has come who can mount a challenge—so clear reason testifies that this can only be through revelation and sending down.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the second intellectual miracle: the Prophet's sudden acquisition of profound knowledge after forty years of silence on these topics. The argument is that if he had studied beforehand, his enemies would have used that against him, claiming he memorized it. They did not, proving he had no prior engagement with such sciences. The fact that he then produced inimitable speech, with no successful challenge for six hundred years, forces reason to conclude it is from divine revelation.

Key Terms
الوحي
التنزيل
المعارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's knowledge came from years of study before his mission.
Correction: The passage proves he did not engage in these topics for forty years, so his sudden knowledge cannot be from study.

Checkpoint
Why does the lack of accusation from enemies prove the Prophet's truthfulness?
A) They would have accused him of learning from others if he had studied
B) They were afraid of him
C) They did not know him
D) They were convinced by his message

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden eloquence after forty years of silence, combined with the inability of others to rival it, proves that his message is from divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Prophet's enemies could not accuse him of studying beforehand. Are there any areas of your life where your actions contradict your words, such that others might justifiably accuse you of hypocrisy? How can you align your deeds with your faith?

Third Intellectual Miracle: Consistency Through Hardship and Power
Imam al-Razi presents the third intellectual miracle: the Prophet's unwavering commitment through hardship and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unwavering commitment to asceticism before and after gaining power serves as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's consistency in hardship and power is impossible for a forger, proving his truthfulness.

Imam al-Razi presents a powerful rational argument: the Prophet (peace be upon him) remained ascetic and committed to his message both when he was weak and when he was strong. This consistency, especially after gaining worldly power, defies the behavior of an imposter. In this lesson, we will examine this third intellectual miracle and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two phases: hardship and then power. Observe the argument's logic.
2
Identify the key contrast
The passage contrasts the Prophet's behavior in two conditions: before victory (hardship) and after victory (power). Focus on the claim that he did not change.
3
Understand the forger argument
The passage argues that a forger would act differently because they seek worldly gain. Once achieved, they would indulge. The Prophet's continued asceticism disproves forgery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث : أنه تحمل في أداء الرسالة أنواعًا من المشاق والمتاعب ، ولم يتغير عن المنهج الأول البتة ، ولم يطمع في مال أحد ولا جاهه ، بل صبر على تلك المشاق والمتاعب ، ولم يظهر في عزمه فتور ولا في إصراره قصور ، ثم إنه لما قهر الأعداء ووجد العسكر العظيم والدولة القاهرة القوية ونفذ أمره في الأموال والأزواج لم يتغير عن منهجه الأول والزهد في الدنيا والإقبال على الآخرة . وكل من أنصف علم أن المزور لا يكون كذلك ، فإن المزور إنما يزور الكذب والباطل على الخلق ليجد الدنيا ، فإذا وجدها ولم ينتفع بها كان ساعيًا في تضييع الدنيا والآخرة على نفسه ، وذلك ما لا يفعله أحد من العقلاء.
The third type: That he bore in delivering the message various kinds of hardships and difficulties, and he did not change from the first path at all, nor did he covet anyone's wealth or status, rather he remained patient upon those hardships and difficulties, and no weakness appeared in his resolve nor deficiency in his persistence. Then, when he overcame the enemies and found great armies and a powerful, strong state, and his authority extended over wealth and wives, he did not change from his first path of asceticism in the world and turning toward the Hereafter. And everyone who is fair-minded knows that a forger cannot be like that, for the forger only forges lies and falsehood upon people to gain the world, so if he gains it and does not benefit from it, he would be striving to waste this world and the Hereafter upon himself, and that is something that none of the rational people would do.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the third intellectual miracle: the Prophet's unwavering commitment to his message and asceticism before and after gaining power. The proof is that an imposter would seek worldly benefit; once he achieves it, he would indulge. The Prophet, however, remained the same in hardship and ease, never deviating from his path. This consistency, despite having the means to enjoy worldly pleasures, is impossible for a liar and thus constitutes a rational miracle.

المزور

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This miracle is about the Prophet's patience in hardship alone.
Correction: It is about his consistency in both hardship and power, which contradicts the behavior of a forger.

Checkpoint
What does the third type argue regarding the Prophet's behavior after gaining power?
A) He became arrogant
B) He remained ascetic and unchanged
C) He increased his wealth
D) He abandoned his message

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unchanged asceticism in both hardship and power is a rational miracle proving his prophethood, as a forger would not forgo worldly gain after achieving it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says a forger would not give up worldly gain after achieving it. Consider a time you compromised truth for some benefit. If you had maintained truthfulness despite the cost, how would your life be different? Are you willing to examine your motives as the passage invites you to?

Prophethood

Proof from Lack of Prior Study
Razi presents the second proof: the Prophet's lack of prior study is proven by his enemies' silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the absence of accusation of prior study serves as a rational proof that the Prophet's knowledge came from revelation.

Core Idea
The enemies' silence is the strongest proof that the Prophet did not study.

Razi presents a clever argument from silence: if the Prophet had studied divine topics before his claim, his enemies would have used that against him. Since they did not, despite their intense eagerness to discredit him, we have strong evidence that his knowledge was divinely given. Let's examine the passage carefully to see how this logic works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the author's own argument structure come through.
The passage is a continuous argument, so read it as a whole.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice the conditional: 'If he had studied, the enemies would have said...' Then the observation: 'They did not say it.' This leads to the conclusion that he did not study.
This is an argumentum e silentio (argument from silence).
3
Reflect on the additional evidence
Razi adds two points: the Prophet was forty years old and had no prior engagement with these topics, and then he produced inimitable speech that no one has challenged in six hundred years.
These strengthen the conclusion that it must be from revelation.
4
Consider why this argument is convincing
Think about the enemies' motives: they had every reason to discredit him. If they could have accused him of studying, they would have. Their silence is therefore significant evidence.
It relies on the principle that absent evidence when expected is evidence of absence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني : أنه لو كان قبل إظهار دعوى الرسالة والنبوة ما كان يشرع في هذه المسائل الإلهية وما كان يبحث عنها وما جرى على لسانه قط حديث النبوة والرسالة. والذي يدل على صحة قولنا : أنه لو اتفق أنه شرع في هذه المطالب والمباحث قبل إظهار ادعاء الرسالة والنبوة لقالت الكفار له : إنك أفنيت عمرك في التدبر والتأمل وتحصيل هذه الكلمات حتى قدرت الآن على إظهارها، ولما لم يذكر هذا الكلام الأعداء من مع شدة حرصهم على الطعن فيه وفي نبوته علمنا أنه ما كان شارعا قبل إظهار النبوة في شيء من هذه العلوم، ومعلوم أن من انقضى من عمره أربعون سنة ولم يخض في شيء من هذه المطالب العلمية ثم إنه خاض بها دفعة واحدة، وأتى بكلام عجز الأولون والآخرون عن معارضته بل قد انقضى الآن قريب من ستمائة سنة وما جاء أحد يمكنه إقامة المعارضة فصريح العقل يشهد بأن هذا لا يكون إلا على سبيل الوحي والتنزيل.
The second type: That if before he manifested the claim of Messengership and Prophethood he had not engaged in these divine matters nor investigated them nor had any talk of prophethood and messengership ever occurred on his tongue. And what proves the correctness of our statement: That if it were to happen that he engaged in these demands and investigations before manifesting the claim of messengership and prophethood, the disbelievers would have said to him: 'You have spent your life in reflection, contemplation, and acquisition of these words until you are now able to manifest them.' And since the enemies did not mention this speech despite their intense eagerness to attack him and his prophethood, we know that he was not engaging in any of these sciences before manifesting prophethood. And it is known that one who has spent forty years of his life and not delved into any of these scientific demands, then he delved into them all at once, and brought speech that the earlier and later generations are incapable of opposing—nay, nearly six hundred years have now passed and no one has come who can mount an opposition—so clear reason bears witness that this cannot be except by way of revelation and divine sending down.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of proof of prophethood, which is an argumentum e silentio. The author (Razi) argues that if the Prophet had studied these divine topics before his claim, his enemies would have used that against him, accusing him of having prepared it. Since they did not, despite their extreme hostility, it proves he had no prior exposure. Razi then emphasizes the improbability: a man of forty who suddenly produces inimitable speech that no one has been able to challenge in six hundred years can only have received it through revelation (al-wahy) and divine sending down (al-tanzil). The proof relies on the fact that the opponents had every motive to discredit him but never used this argument.

Key Terms
النوع الثاني
دعوى الرسالة
الوحي
التنزيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this argument is circular, because it assumes the enemies would have known about any prior study.
Correction: The argument is not circular; it relies on the external fact that the enemies had every motive to discredit him and would have used any available evidence. Their silence is an independent observation that supports the conclusion.

Checkpoint
What is the key evidence in the second type that the Prophet did not study these matters before prophethood?
A) The enemies accused him of studying
B) The enemies did not accuse him of studying despite their eagerness to attack
C) The Prophet was illiterate
D) The Quran is inimitable

Key Takeaway
The enemies' failure to accuse the Prophet of prior study, despite their eagerness to discredit him, proves that his knowledge came solely from revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were among those enemies with the same intense eagerness to disprove the Prophet, what accusation would you have made? Their silence proves they had none. What does their silence reveal about your own resistance to submitting to the truth?
?
The Prophet spent forty years without studying these matters, yet produced speech that no one can oppose. How do you account for this in your own life? Will you attribute it to revelation, or do you still invent excuses?
?
What are the silences in your own heart when faced with clear truth? What do you avoid acknowledging about the proofs of prophethood, and what is holding you back from full certainty?

Proof from Consistent Asceticism
Razi argues that the Prophet's consistent asceticism proves his sincerity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unwavering asceticism, both in hardship and after victory, serves as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Consistency of character in power and poverty proves truthfulness.

This lesson examines the third type of proof for prophethood presented by Imam Razi. He argues that the Prophet's unwavering asceticism, both during times of hardship and after gaining victory, demonstrates his sincerity. Razi contrasts this with the behavior of an impostor, who would seek worldly gain.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two main parts: the description of the Prophet's conduct and the logical contrast with an impostor.
The passage is dense; take your time to understand each phrase.
2
Identify the key claim
The key claim is that the Prophet did not change his asceticism after gaining power. Why is this significant? It shows his message was not for worldly gain.
3
Understand the contrast
Razi uses the example of an impostor (muzawwir). What would an impostor do? He would seek worldly gain and thus change his behavior once he obtains it. The Prophet's consistency proves he is not an impostor.
This is a logical deduction: if he were an impostor, he would have changed.
4
Reflect on the misunderstanding
Consider the common misunderstanding that wealth contradicts asceticism. How does Razi address this? The Prophet had wealth but did not change his lifestyle.
This demonstrates that asceticism is about detachment, not poverty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث : أنه تحمل في أداء الرسالة أنواعًا من المشاق والمتاعب ، لا ولم يتغير عن المنهج الأول ،البتة، ولم يطمع في مال أحد ولا جاهه، بل صبر على تلك المشاق والمتاعب، ولم يظهر في عزمه فتور ولا في إصراره قصور، ثم إنه لما قهر الأعداء ووجد العسكر العظيم والدولة القاهرة القوية ونفذ أمره في الأموال والأزواج لم يتغير عن منهجه الأول والزهد في الدنيا والإقبال على الآخرة. وكل من أنصف علم أن المزور لا يكون كذلك، فإن المزور إنما يزور الكذب والباطل على الخلق ليجد الدنيا، فإذا وجدها ولم ينتفع بها كان ساعيًا في تضييع الدنيا والآخرة على نفسه، وذلك ما لا يفعله أحد من العقلاء.
The third type: That he endured in delivering the message types of hardships and troubles, and he did not change from the first path at all, nor did he covet anyone's wealth or status. Rather he patiently endured those hardships and troubles, and no languor appeared in his resolve nor any deficiency in his persistence. Then when he overcame the enemies and found great armies and a strong, victorious state, and his command was executed in wealth and wives, he did not change from his first path of asceticism in this world and turning towards the hereafter. And everyone who is fair knows that an impostor is not like that. For the impostor only forges lies and falsehood against people to gain the world; so if he gains it and yet does not benefit from it, he is striving to waste this world and the hereafter on himself. And that is something no rational person would do.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the third type of proof, based on the Prophet's character. Razi argues that the Prophet endured great hardships in delivering his message, never deviating from his path, and without seeking wealth or status. After gaining victory, power, and wealth, he did not change his ascetic lifestyle (zuhd) and focus on the afterlife. Razi then contrasts this with an impostor (al-muzawwir), who would seek worldly gain. If an impostor obtained the world but did not use it, he would lose both this world and the hereafter—something no rational person would do. Therefore, the Prophet's consistency proves his truthfulness.

Key Terms
النوع الثالث
المشاق
الزهد
المزور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet's later wealth contradicts asceticism, implying he was not truly ascetic.
Correction: Razi argues that the Prophet's lifestyle did not change despite having wealth; asceticism is about detachment, not poverty.

Checkpoint
What does the third type argue about the Prophet after he gained power?
A) He became less religious
B) He continued his asceticism and did not change his path
C) He indulged in worldly pleasures
D) He abandoned his mission

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's consistent asceticism before and after victory disproves the possibility of imposture and confirms his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a success—whether in wealth, status, or relationships—do you find yourself drifting from your spiritual commitments? The Prophet did not. What does that say about the depth of your faith? This week, identify one area where you have changed for the worse after gaining something, and make a concrete plan to return to your original path.
?
If you were given absolute power over your domain (family, workplace, community) tomorrow, would your character remain the same? Or would you begin to justify compromises? The Prophet's consistency is a proof of his truthfulness. Your inconsistency is a proof of your need for self-reformation. What is one small habit you can practice daily to anchor your character regardless of circumstances?
?
The impostor wastes both worlds when he gains the world but does not enjoy it. Are you living in a way that makes you an impostor in your own faith—appearing religious but pursuing the world? Examine your heart: does your worship increase when you are tested, and decrease when you are comfortable? Commit to one act of worship that you will maintain whether you are in ease or hardship.

Proof from Previous Scriptures
Razi enumerates the fifth proof and supports it with Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the claim of prophetic foretelling in previous scriptures as a proof of prophethood, and the logical challenge it presents to the People of the Book.

Core Idea
The Prophet's claim to be foretold in Torah and Gospel was a challenge no one could refute.

Razi introduces a fifth type of proof: the glad tidings of the Prophet's coming in the Torah and Gospel. He cites Quranic verses that assert the Prophet is mentioned there, and implies that if this claim were false, the People of the Book would have refuted it. This passage highlights how the Prophet used existing scriptures to validate his mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: Razi states the proof type, provides the evidence (Quranic verses), and ends with an implied challenge.
The passage ends abruptly; the implied conclusion is that the People of the Book would have exposed a lie.
2
Identify the four Quranic verses
Find each verse cited by Razi. Note the key themes: the Prophet written in Torah and Gospel, Jesus foretelling Ahmad, rebuke for disbelieving while witnessing, and recognition like one's own sons.
These verses are from Surahs Al-A'raf, As-Saff, Al 'Imran, and Al-Baqarah.
3
Understand the logical argument
Razi argues that the Prophet's claim was public and the People of the Book, who possessed the scriptures, did not refute it. Their silence implies the claim's truth.
This is a form of argument from silence or challenge.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Some might think this proof depends on the current scriptures' authenticity, but Razi uses it as a challenge: the contemporaries failed to disprove the claim.
The argument is about the immediate challenge, not textual integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الخامس من دلائل نبوته ورود البشارة بمقدمه العزيز في التوراة والإنجيل والدليل علي ذلك أنه ادعى أن ذكره موجود في التوراة والإنجيل، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النبى الأمى الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَةِ والإنجيل [الأعراف: ١٥٧] وقال تعالى حكاية عن المسيح ومشرا بِرَسُول يأتي من بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحَدٌ﴾ [الصف: ٦] وقال: ﴿يَتأَهْلَ الْكِتَبِ لِمَ تَكْفُرُونَ بِشَايَاتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنتُمْ تَشْهَدُونَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ٧٠] وقال: ﴿ الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَهُمُ الْكِتَبَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ١٤٦] ومعلوم أنه لو كان كاذبًا في ذلك لكان هذا من أعظم
The fifth type of proofs of his prophethood: the occurrence of glad tidings of his noble coming in the Torah and the Gospel. The evidence for that is that he claimed that his mention is present in the Torah and the Gospel. Allah says: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' (Al-A'raf 7:157). And Allah said, narrating from the Messiah: 'And giving good tidings of a Messenger who will come after me, whose name is Ahmad' (As-Saff 61:6). And He said: 'O People of the Scripture, why do you disbelieve in the verses of Allah while you witness?' (Al 'Imran 3:70). And He said: 'Those to whom We gave the Scripture know him as they know their own sons' (Al-Baqarah 2:146). And it is known that if he were lying in that, this would be among the greatest...
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth type of proof: the glad tidings (al-bishara) of the Prophet's coming in the Torah and Gospel. Razi argues that the Prophet himself claimed that his mention is present in these scriptures, and then cites four Quranic verses to support this: (1) Al-A'raf 7:157 – describing the unlettered prophet written in Torah and Gospel; (2) As-Saff 61:6 – Jesus announcing a messenger named Ahmad; (3) Al 'Imran 3:70 – rebuking the People of the Scripture for disbelieving while they witness; (4) Al-Baqarah 2:146 – that they recognize him as they recognize their own sons. Razi then implies that if the Prophet were lying, the People of the Book would have exposed him, but they did not. The passage ends mid-sentence with 'this would be among the greatest...'.

Key Terms
النوع الخامس
البشارة
التوراة
الإنجيل
أحمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof depends on the current Torah and Gospel being authentic and unchanged.
Correction: Razi's argument is about the challenge: the contemporaries of the Prophet, who had the scriptures (in their form at that time), did not refute his claim. It is a proof from their silence, not from textual integrity.

Checkpoint
According to the fifth type, what is the evidence that the Prophet's prophethood was foretold?
A) The Prophet performed miracles
B) The Quran claims his mention is in the Torah and Gospel
C) The enemies admitted it
D) The Prophet studied ancient texts

Key Takeaway
The glad tidings in previous scriptures serve as a proof because the Prophet's claim was public and the People of the Book could have refuted it but did not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that the People of the Book knew the Prophet as they know their own sons. Do you know him with that same level of certainty? If not, what is holding you back from deeper conviction, and what will you do today to remove it?
?
The Prophet’s public claim was never refuted by those who had the scriptures. Have you ever presented this proof to a Jew or Christian you know? If not, what is preventing you from doing so, and what would change if you took that risk?
?
This argument is a challenge to the People of the Book, but it is also a mirror for you: if you truly believe this proof, does your daily life reflect absolute certainty in his prophethood? Where do you still act as if you have doubts, and how will you address that gap starting now?

Quranic Prophecies as Multi-Layered Proofs
Razi enumerates three Quranic prophecies and their theological implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how specific Quranic prophecies serve as evidence for God's knowledge, power, Muhammad's prophethood, and the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

Core Idea
Quranic prophecies are multi-layered proofs that confirm divine attributes and the truth of Islam.

Razi presents three concrete examples of Quranic prophecies that were fulfilled historically. These verses not only confirm Muhammad's prophethood but also demonstrate God's perfect knowledge and power, and even support the caliphate of the Companions. Let's examine how these verses serve as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to understand the basic meaning.
The passage is enumerative, listing three prophecies.
2
Identify the three prophecies
Find each prophecy mentioned by Razi: the first from verse 24:55, the second from 62:6-7, the third from 2:61. Notice what each prophecy predicted.
3
Understand the multiple conclusions drawn from each
For the first prophecy, Razi draws four conclusions: God's knowledge, power, Muhammad's prophethood, and the caliphate. See how he reasons from the verse to each point.
4
Reflect on the cumulative force of these prophecies
Consider how multiple fulfilled prophecies strengthen the case for Islam and its teachings.
This connects to the broader argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثلاثون. الْأَرْضِ ﴾ [النور: ٥٥] والمراد منه الصحابة، بدليل قوله: ﴿ وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّن بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا ﴾ وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام، فهذه الآية دالة على كون صانع العالم سبحانه عالما بكل المعلومات؛ لأنه تعالى أخبر عما سيأتي، ثم كان الأمر كما أخبره، وعلى كونه تعالى قادرًا على كل الممكنات؛ لأنه وعد بالنصرة التامة وقد وقعت، وعلى نبوة محمد ﷺ لأنه استبد بذكر هذا الغيب فلا بد أن يكون ذلك الله، وعلى خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين لأنه تعالى قال: ﴿ وَلَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ [النور: ٥٥] فوعد بالخلافة جمعًا من الحاضرين في ذلك الوقت وأقل الجمع ثلاثة. وتاسعها: قوله تعالى: ﴿ قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا ﴾ [الجمعة: ٦] إلى قوله: ﴿ وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا بِمَا قَدَّمَتْ أَيْدِيهِمْ ﴾ [الجمعة: ٧] ثم كان كما أخبر. وعاشرها: قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الذِّلَّةُ وَالْمَسْكَنَةُ ﴾ [البقرة: ٦١] وظهور ذلك في اليهود معلوم فإنه ما رفعت لهم راية قط وما ظهر فيهم سلطان ولا قاهر.
The thirtieth issue. '...the earth...' [Q 24:55] and the intended meaning is the Companions, by evidence of His saying: 'And He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security.' And they were the fearful ones in early Islam. So this verse indicates that the Maker of the world, exalted, is knowing of all known things because He informed of what would come, and then the matter was as He informed; and that He is powerful over all possible things because He promised complete victory and it occurred; and the prophethood of Muhammad ﷺ because he singled out mentioning this unseen, so it must be from Allah; and the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs because He said: 'And He will surely establish them in the land' [Q 24:55], so He promised caliphate to a group of those present at that time, and the least of a group is three. The ninth: His saying: 'Say, O you who are Jews...' [Q 62:6] to His saying: '...and they will never wish for it because of what their hands have put forth' [Q 62:7], then it was as He informed. The tenth: His saying: 'And they were struck with humiliation and poverty' [Q 2:61], and the manifestation of that among the Jews is known, for they never raised a banner and no authority or conqueror appeared among them.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage presents two examples of Quranic prophecies as evidence for various theological points. The first example is from verse 24:55, which is interpreted as referring to the Companions. The verse promises that after fear they will be given security and established in the land. Razi argues that this verse demonstrates: (1) that God is all-knowing because He predicted future events which came true; (2) that God is all-powerful because He fulfilled His promise; (3) the prophethood of Muhammad because he alone reported this unseen; and (4) the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs because the promise was made to a group (at least three) of those present. The second example is verse 62:6-7, where the Jews are challenged to wish for death, but they never do; this prediction also came true. The third example is verse 2:61, which states that the Jews were struck with humiliation and poverty; Razi notes that this is manifestly true as they never had political power. These are presented as proofs of prophethood and divine attributes.

Key Terms
الآيات القرآنية
النبوة
الخلافة
الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these verses only prove prophethood.
Correction: Razi uses them also to prove divine knowledge, power, and the caliphate.

Checkpoint
How does Razi use the verse 'وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّن بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا' (24:55) to prove the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs?
A) It promises caliphate to a single person
B) It promises caliphate to a group of at least three
C) It promises victory after fear
D) It mentions the Companions by name

Key Takeaway
Quranic prophecies are powerful evidence that affirm God's attributes and the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the Companions' fear turning to security, do you truly believe that God's promises are as certain today? What fear in your life are you holding onto instead of trusting His guarantee?
?
The Jews were challenged to wish for death if they were truly God's beloved—yet they never did. If you were in their place, would your actions match your claimed faith? What does your daily life reveal about your love for meeting God?
?
These prophecies were fulfilled with precision. But have you ever read the Quran and felt its words were merely historical, not a living address to you right now? What would change today if you took this passage as a direct sign for your own certainty? How will you respond?

Non-Quranic Prophecies: Ten Evidences of Prophethood
Razi enumerates ten non-Quranic prophecies from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand ten specific hadith-based prophecies that prove the truthfulness of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ and how they serve as evidence for his prophethood.

Core Idea
Ten verifiable prophecies in hadith confirm Muhammad's prophethood.

Imam Razi presents ten reported prophecies from the Prophet ﷺ that were fulfilled exactly as stated. These examples are not from the Quran but from authentic hadith, and each one serves as a clear miracle in the form of news of the unseen. By examining these prophecies, we see how the Prophet's knowledge of future events confirms his divine mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: each prophecy is introduced with a number.
Take your time; the list is long but each item is self-contained.
2
Identify the fulfillment
For each prophecy, identify how it was fulfilled. Razi often adds 'and it was as he said' or similar.
Pay attention to the details, e.g., the specific people and places.
3
Reflect on cumulative evidence
Consider how these ten examples build a strong case for prophethood. Also note Razi's comment about the Quran being a stronger report (khabar) for the caliphate of Abu Bakr.
This step connects the lesson to broader theological method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإخبار عن الغيوب المستقبلة في غير القرآن فكثير: أحدها: قوله ﷺ: «زويت لي الأرض فأريت مشارقها ومغاربها، وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوي لي منها» وكان الأمر كما أخبر. وثانيها: قوله لعدي بن حاتم: «كيف بك إذا خرجت الظعينة من أقصى اليمن إلى أقصى الحيرة لا تخاف إلا الله؟!». وثالثها: أنه أخبر أصحابه يموت النجاشي وصلى عليه، ثم شاعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ورابعها: قوله: «عمار بن ياسر تقتلك الفئة الباغية» فقتل مع علي يوم صفين، وهذا يدل على توحيد الله ونبوة محمد ﷺ وخلافة علي له إلا أنه خبر، ودليل خلافة أبي بكر قرآن، والقرآن خبر من الخبر. وخامسها: قوله لعلي: «أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة والذي يخضب هذه من هذه» يعني الذي يضرب على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك، ثم كان كما قال فضرب على رأسه فقتله. وسادسها: قوله ﷺ لعلي: «ستقاتل الناكثين والقاسطين والمارقين». وسابعها: قوله ﷺ: «اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر» وكان هذا إخبارًا عن بقائهما بعده. وثامنها: قوله: «الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة» وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين هذا القدر. وتاسعها: ليلة الإسراء فإنه أخبر قريشًا عن أمور فكانت كما أخبر. وعاشرها: قوله للعباس حين أسره: «افد نفسك وابني أخيك عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارث، فإنك ذو مال» فقال: لا مال عندي، فقال: «أين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا ولعبد الله كذا ولفلان كذا؟» فقال العباس: والذي بعثك بالحق نبيًا ما علم هذا أحد غيري وإنك لرسول الله، وأسلم هو وعقيل. واعلم أن معجزات النبي ﷺ كثيرة، واكتفينا ههنا بهذا القدر.
As for reports about future unseen matters in other than the Quran, they are many: First: His saying ﷺ: 'The earth was folded for me, and I was shown its easts and wests, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me of it.' And it was as he informed. Second: His saying to 'Adi ibn Hatim: 'How are you when a woman riding a howdah will go from the farthest Yemen to the farthest al-Hirah, fearing none but Allah?!' Third: That he informed his Companions that the Negus would die and he prayed over him, then news spread that he died that day. Fourth: His saying: ''Ammar ibn Yasir will be killed by the transgressing group.' So he was killed with 'Ali on the day of Siffin. This indicates the oneness of Allah, the prophethood of Muhammad ﷺ, and the caliphate of 'Ali, except that it is a report (khabar), while the evidence for the caliphate of Abu Bakr is the Quran, and the Quran is a stronger report. Fifth: His saying to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' – meaning the one who will strike your head and dye your beard with the blood of your head. Then it was as he said, so he was struck on his head and killed. Sixth: His saying ﷺ to 'Ali: 'You will fight the breakers of the covenant, the unjust, and the deviators.' Seventh: His saying ﷺ: 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar,' and this was an informing of their survival after him. Eighth: His saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' and the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was that amount. Ninth: The Night Journey, for he informed Quraysh about matters and they were as he informed. Tenth: His saying to al-'Abbas when he was captured: 'Ransom yourself and the two sons of your brother, 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith, for you are a man of wealth.' He said: I have no wealth. He said: 'Where is the wealth you left in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl when no one else was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then for al-Fadl such and such, for 'Abdullah such and such, and for so-and-so such and such?' Al-'Abbas said: By the One who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this but me, and indeed you are the Messenger of Allah. So he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And know that the miracles of the Prophet ﷺ are many, and we suffice with this amount here.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage lists ten prophecies from the Prophet ﷺ that are not in the Quran. Each one demonstrates his truthfulness. The first is the hadith about the earth being folded and the future expansion of the Muslim empire. The second predicts the safe travel of women. The third is the death of the Negus. The fourth predicts the death of 'Ammar ibn Yasir at the hands of a transgressing group, which occurred at Siffin. Razi notes that this also supports 'Ali's caliphate, but he distinguishes between report (khabar) and Quranic evidence. The fifth is the prophecy about the one who would strike 'Ali. The sixth predicts 'Ali's battles against three groups. The seventh commands following Abu Bakr and 'Umar. The eighth limits the caliphate to thirty years. The ninth is the Night Journey. The tenth is the specific knowledge of the hidden wealth of al-'Abbas. Razi concludes that the Prophet's miracles are many and that this list suffices.

Key Terms
معجزة
إخبار عن الغيب
النبوة
الخبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These prophecies are merely stories that could be coincidences.
Correction: Each prophecy is a specific, verifiable prediction of future events that were fulfilled exactly as stated, which cannot be attributed to coincidence and serve as clear miracles.

Checkpoint
Which example does Razi use to argue that the Quran is stronger evidence than hadith?
A) The prophecy about 'Ammar's death
B) The prophecy about the caliphate duration
C) The prophecy about al-'Abbas's hidden wealth

Key Takeaway
Ten hadith prophecies, each fulfilled exactly, provide compelling evidence for Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet knew the exact details of al-Abbas’s hidden wealth. Does your private life reflect a belief that the Prophet’s knowledge extends to your secrets? What secret are you hiding that you need to bring to the light today?
?
These prophecies were witnessed and confirmed by those present. Your life is witnessed by Allah and His angels. Are you living as if the Day of Judgment is as certain as the fulfillment of these prophecies? Name one small habit you will change today to align your actions with that certainty.
